florence municipal code ____________ 1979 ____________ a codification of the general ordinances of the city of florence colorado ____________ beginning with supp no 12 109 supplemented by municipal ____________ > preface the florence municipal originally published by book publishing company in 197 has been kept current by regular supplementation by matthew bender & company inc its successor in interest during original codification the ordinances were compiled edited and indexed by the editorial staff of book publishing company under the direction of william g cox borough manager beginning with supplement 12 109 municipal will be keeping this by regular supplementation the code is organized by subject matter under an expandable threefactor decimal numbering system which is designed to facilitate supplementation without disturbing the numbering of existing provisions each section number designates in sequence the numbers of the title chapter and section thus located in of title 2 in most instances sections are numbered by tens 010 020 030 etc leaving nine vacant positions between original sections to accommodate future provisions similarly chapters and titles are numbered to provide for internal expansion in parentheses following each section is a legislative history identifying the specific sources for the provisions of that section this legislative history is complemented by an ordinance disposition table following the text of the code listing by number all ordinances their subjects and where they appear in the codification  and beginning with supplement no 12 109 legislation can be tracked using the table and disposition list a subjectmatter index with complete crossreferencing locates specific code provisions by individual section numbers this supplement brings the to date a passed  municipal capital circle sw tallahassee fl 32310 8002622633 how to use your code this organized to make the laws of the city as accessible as possible to city officials city employees and private citizens please take a moment to familiarize yourself with some of the important elements of this system the numbering system is the backbone of a ordinances  municipal uses a unique and versatile numbering structure that allows for easy expansion and amendment of this is based on three tiers beginning with title then chapter and ending with section each part is represented in the code section number for example in of title 2 title a title is a broad category under which ordinances on a related subject are compiled this about 15 to 20 titles for example the first title is title 1 general provisions which may contain ordinances about the general penalty code adoption and definitions the titles in this separated by tabbed divider pages for quick reference some titles are reserved for later use deal with more specific subjects and are often derived from one ordinance all of the chapters on a related subject are grouped in one title the chapters are numbered so that new chapters which should logically be placed near certain existing chapters can be added at a later time without renumbering existing material for example city manager can be added between 204 city council and city attorney section of the code contains substantive ordinance material the sections are numbered by tens to allow for expansion of the code without renumbering tables of contents there are many tables of contents in this assist in locating specific information at the beginning of the code is the main table of contents listing each title in addition each title and chapter has its own table of contents listing the chapters and sections respectively note at the end of each code section you will find an ordinance history note which lists the underlying ordinances for that section the ordinances are listed by number section if applicable and year example  1992 beginning with supplement no 12 109 a secondary ordinance history note will be appended to affected sections notes will be amended with the most recent ordinance added to the end these history notes can be cross referenced to the code comparative table and disposition list appearing at the back of the volume preceding the index statutory references the statutory references direct the code user to those portions of the state statutes that are applicable to the laws of the municipality as the statutes are revised these references will be updated crossreference table when a code is based on an earlier codification the crossreference table will help users find older or prior code references in the new code the crossreference table is located near the end of the code under the tabbed divider tables this table lists the prior code section in the column labeled prior  and the new code section in the column labeled herein as of supplement no 12 109 this table will no longer be updated disposition table to find a specific ordinance in the code turn to the section called tables for the disposition table this very useful table tells you the status of every ordinance reviewed for inclusion in the code the table is organized by ordinance number and provides a brief description and the disposition of the ordinance if the ordinance is codified the chapter or chapters will be indicated example 204 612 904 if the ordinance is of a temporary nature or deals with subjects not normally codified such as budgets taxes annexations or rezones the disposition will be not codified if the ordinance is for some reason omitted from the code usually at the direction of the municipality the disposition will be not codified other dispositions sometimes used are tabled pending number not used or missing beginning with supplement no 12 109 this table will be replaced with the table and disposition list table and disposition list beginning with supplement no 12 109 a table and disposition list has been added for use in tracking legislative history located in the back of this volume this table is a chronological listing of each ordinance considered for codification the table and disposition list specifies the ordinance number adoption date description of the ordinance and the disposition within the code of each ordinance by use of the table and disposition list the reader can locate any section of the code as supplemented and any subsequent ordinance included herein index if you are not certain where to look for a particular subject in this code start with the index this is an alphabetical multitier subject index which uses section numbers as the reference and crossreferences where necessary look for the main heading of the subject you need then the appropriate subheadings business license see also business tax fee  required when  the index will be updated as necessary when the code text is amended instruction sheet each supplement to the new code will be accompanied by an instruction sheet the instruction sheet will tell the code user the date of the most recent supplement and the last ordinance contained in that supplement it will then list the pages that must be pulled from the code and the new pages that must be inserted following these instructions carefully will assure that the code is kept accurate and current removed pages should be kept for future reference page numbers when originally published the pages of this consecutively numbered as of supplement no 12 109 when new pages are inserted with amendments the pages will follow a point numbering system example 32 321 322   33 backs of pages that are blank in codes that are printed doublesided will be left unnumbered but the number will be reserved for later use electronic submission in the interests of accuracy and speed we encourage you to submit your ordinances electronically if at all possible we can accept most any file format including word wordperfect or text files if you have a choice we prefer word any version you can send files to us as an email attachment by ftp on a diskette or cdrom electronic files enable us not only to get you your code more quickly but also ensure that it is errorfree our email address is ords@municodecom  for hard copy send one copy of all ordinances passed to municipal po box 2235 tallahassee fl 32316 customer service if you have any questions about this our services please contact 219 02042019a 3 42019 omitted 27 219 title 1  general provisions code adoption   purpose the code of the city of florence as promulgated by the city of florence colorado is adopted and enacted by reference the purpose of this code is to codify the ordinances of the city which are of a general and permanent nature the subject matter of this code includes provisions concerning the application and interpretation of the code the administration and organization of the city animals buildings abandoned automobiles peddlers finances streets nuisances traffic offenses civil defense elections and zoning  1980   primary and secondary codes and building standards adopted by reference the following primary and secondary codes and building standards are adopted by reference as if the same were set forth in full in this code a the model traffic colorado municipalities revised 1995 edition published by the colorado department of transportation save and except for such amendments as are set forth at b the international building edition promulgated by the international save and except for such amendments as are set forth at c the international residential edition promulgated by the international save and except for such amendments as are set forth at d the international mechanical edition promulgated by the international save and except for such amendments as are set forth at e the international energy edition promulgated by the international save and except for such amendments as are set forth at f the international existing building edition promulgated by the international save and except for such amendments as are set forth at g flood damage prevention resolution 52007 as the official flood plain development resolution of the city of florence h flood insurance rate maps dated  published by the federal emergency management agency i the standard construction specifications and standard details for the city of pueblo colorado revised  edition also known as the florence street standards save and except for such amendments as are set forth at  2008   titlecitationreference this code shall be known as the florence municipal it shall be sufficient to refer to such code in any prosecution for the violation of any provision thereof or in any proceeding at law or equity it shall be sufficient to designate any ordinance adding to amending correcting or repealing all or any portion thereof as an addition to amendment to correction or repeal of the florence municipal reference may be had to the title chapters sections and subsections of the florence municipal such references shall apply to that numbered title chapter section or subsection as it appears in the code  1980   ordinances passed prior to adoption of coderepeal of certain ordinances a the last ordinance included in the initial florence municipal the following ordinances passed subsequent to but prior to adoption of this code are adopted and made a part of this code ordinances no 579   ordinances no 1089 b all ordinances and parts of ordinances of a primary and general nature passed prior to  and in effect at the time the florence municipal adopted but not included in said code are repealed ordinances passed on or after  shall not be repealed or amended by the adoption of the florence municipal the ordinance codified in this chapter and  1980   matters not affected by repeal the repeal of ordinances and pats of ordinances by the ordinance codified in this chapter and shall not affect any offense committed or act done any penalty or forfeiture incurred or any contract right or obligation established prior to the time when said ordinances and parts of ordinances are repealed  1980   ordinances saved from repeal the repeal of ordinances of a general and permanent nature by the ordinance codified in this chapter and shall not repeal any ordinance or part thereof saved from repeal specifically by the florence municipal nor shall such repeal affect any ordinance a promising guaranteeing or authorizing the payment of money by or for the city  b authorizing or relating to specific issuances of bonds or other evidences of indebtedness  c granting a franchise  d establishing the compensation of city officers or employees  e levying taxes making appropriations or adopting a budget  f creating specific local improvement districts  g making special assessments for local improvements  h vacating accepting establishing locating relocating or opening any street or public way  i affecting the corporate limits of the city  j which is of a special or temporary nature  k dedicating or accepting any plat or subdivision  1980   severability of code provisions if any sections section subsection or provision of this code of ordinances or the application thereof to any person or circumstances is declared unconstitutional or otherwise invalid by any competent court such invalidity shall not affect the other sections subsections provisions or applications of this code if they can be given effect without the invalid sections section subsection provision or application  1980   codes kept on file a at least three 3 copies of the florence municipal of each secondary code adopted in all certified by the mayor and the city clerk to be true copies of such codes as they were adopted by this ordinance shall be kept on file in the office of the city clerk available for public inspection one copy of each such code may be kept in the office of the chief enforcement officer thereof rather than in the office of the clerk b the city clerk shall prepare and publish revised sheets of every looseleaf page in need of revision by reason of amendment addition or repeal the city clerk shall distribute said revised looseleaf sheets for such fee as the city council may direct c in addition to those copies of this code specified in subsection a of this section a copy of this code shall be kept on file in the office of the city clerk in which it shall be the express duty of the city clerk to insert in their designated places all amendments or ordinances which are intended to become a part of the florence municipal the same have been printed or reprinted in page form and to extract from such code all provisions which may from time to time be repealed this copy of the florence municipal be available to all persons desiring to examine it and shall be considered the official florence municipal the city of florence  1980   sale of code copies the city clerk shall maintain a reasonable supply of copies of this code to be available for purchase by the public at a moderate price  1980 city seal footnotes  1  for statutory provisions on the city seal see crs 1973  314110 1975 supp   seal designated a seal the impression of which is as follows in the center the picture of an oil derrick and the word seal and around the outer edge the words florence freemont co col incorporated sept 7 188 shall be and hereby is declared to be seal of the city of florence  1901 wards footnotes  2  for statutory provisions requiring the division of the city into wards see crs 1973  314l04 1975 supp   statutory authorization the ordinance codified in this chapter is authorized by the provisions of of the colorado revised statutes 1973 as amended  1980   ward one all that portion of the city lying east of the hereinafter described line shall be and constitute ward one beginning at the intersection of the north line of the city limits with the center of north robinson avenue  thence southerly along the centerline of north robinson avenue to its common point with south robinson avenue also known as colorado state highway 67 to the south line of the city limits  1980   722012   ward two all that portion of the city lying west of the boundary of ward one and east of the hereinafter described line shall be and constitute ward two beginning at the intersection of the northern city limits with the center of west seventh street  thence westerly along the centerline of west seventh street to its intersection with north santa fe avenue  thence southerly along the centerline of north santa fe avenue to its intersection with west second street  thence westerly along west second street to its intersection with church avenue  thence southeasterly along the centerline of church avenue to its intersection with west main street  thence westerly along west main street to its intersection with denver street  thence southeasterly along the centerline of denver street and continuing straight along an extension of the centerline of denver street to its intersection with south union street  thence southerly along south union street to its intersection with moore drive  thence southwesterly along the centerline of moore drive to the south line of the city limits  1980   722012   ward three all of that portion of the city lying west of the western boundary of ward two as described in shall be and constitute ward three  1980   722012 general penalty   general penalty provision a any person firm or corporation who violates any provision of this code of ordinances by doing any act prohibited or declared to be unlawful thereby or declared to be an offense or misdemeanor thereby or who fails to do any act required by any such provision or who fails to do any act when such provision declares such failure to be unlawful or to be an offense or misdemeanor or who pursues any business trade or calling or does any act for which a license permit or certificate is required thereby without having a valid license permit or certificate in effect shall be guilty of a misdemeanor  and upon conviction thereof shall be punished by a fine not exceeding two thousand six hundred fifty dollars $265000 unless a specific penalty is provided for a particular misdemeanor plus court costs and any surcharges adopted by the city council each day upon which any such violation continues shall constitute a separate misdemeanor b the limitation on municipal court fines set forth in paragraph a above shall be adjusted for inflation in  and on january 1 of each year thereafter pursuant to crs 1310113 as amended  1992  852013   secondary code infraction provisions a infractions of the secondary codes adopted by reference by the florence municipal set forth in except for infractions of the model traffic colorado municipalities which are treated at shall be a civil matter and result in a fine as set forth in subsection b of this section any penalty provisions contained within such secondary codes are expressly repealed in their entirety b any person firm or corporation who violates any provision of any secondary code codified at except for infractions of the model traffic colorado municipalities by doing any act prohibited or declared to be an infraction thereof or who fails to do any act required by any such provision or who fails to do any act when such provision declares such failure to be an infraction or who pursues any business trade or calling or does any act for which a license permit or certificate is required thereby without having a valid license permit or certificate in effect shall be subject to a fine not exceeding four hundred ninetynine dollars $49900 each day upon which any such infraction continues shall constitute a separate infraction  1993 title 2  administration and personnel administrative organization footnotes  1  for statutory provisions on the city manager form of government see crs 1973  314201 et seq 1975 supp   to govern from and after the date of final passage and approval of the ordinance codified in this chapter all administration of city affairs shall be provided in this chapter  1952   powers of city council the city council shall be the body of final responsibility and shall have all powers and be subject to such responsibilities and limitations which may now or hereafter be granted or imposed by law  1952   powers of city manager the city manager shall be the chief administrative officer of the city and shall be responsible solely to the city council for all affairs placed in his charge by law ordinance or direction of the city council  1952   city attorney and police magistrate the city attorney and the police magistrate shall be under the supervision of the city council and shall perform such duties as are imposed by law ordinance or direction of the city council  1952   city managerdepartmental control all departments of the city except for the city attorney and the police magistrate shall be under the direct control and supervision of the city manager  1952   city managerauthority the city manager is granted authority to establish such methods of handling details of administration as will in his opinion best promote efficiency in the municipal government  1952   departmentscreated there are created the following departments a the department of finance which shall be supervised by the city clerk which officer shall be exofficio city treasurer and clerk of the council the city clerk as supervisor of the department of finance shall keep and supervise all accounts and have custody of all public moneys of the city  apportion and collect special assessments  issue licenses  collect license fees  issue water statements  collect water accounts  make and keep a journal of proceedings of the council  have custody of all public records of the city not specifically entrusted to any other office  and perform such other duties as may now or hereafter be assigned by law ordinance or the city manager  b the department of police which shall be under the supervision and direction of a chief of police the department of police shall cause the public peace of the city to be preserved and shall enforce all laws and ordinances and shall carry out other duties at the direction of the city manager  c the department of fire which shall be a volunteer department headed by a fire chief who shall be responsible for the supervision and direction of the department and for the prevention and suppression of fires and who shall perform other duties as the city manager may direct  d the department of public works which shall be supervised and directed by a director of public works the department of public works shall be responsible for the management maintenance repair and construction of all property of the city except as provided elsewhere in this code any function or activity of the municipality not included elsewhere in this shall come under the supervision of this department  e the cemetery department supervised by a sexton the functions of which department shall include cemetery construction maintenance landscaping and other necessary duties  f health department which shall be headed by a sanitarian which department shall perform all functions relating to the general health of the city  1952   departmentsresponsibilities all of the department created in be under the direct control of the city manager and shall be responsible to him and in addition to the functions and duties herein described for them they shall perform such duties as are now or hereafter assigned by law ordinance or the city manager  1952   appointment of deputies the city manager is granted authority to appoint deputies to the department heads referred to in which deputies shall have the authority given their superiors in the event the heads of departments shall be absent or unable to act  1952 city council footnotes  2  for statutory provisions on city council meetings see crs 1973  314101 1975 supp and  3141071 1975 supp  for provisions on public meetings see crs 1973  299101  for provisions on councilmen generally see crs 1973  314106 et seq and  314205 et seq 1975 supp   meeting dates the regular meetings of the city council of the city of florence shall be held on the first and third mondays of each month    councilmembersterms a councilmembersnumber the city council shall consist of seven 7 members which number shall include the mayor and two members from each ward in the city elected in accordance with the provisions of this chapter b mayor the mayor shall be elected from the city at large by a plurality of votes cast for that office at the regular municipal election held in november of oddnumbered years the mayor shall serve for a term of two 2 years c councilmembers there shall be two 2 councilmembers elected from each ward each of which shall serve a four 4 year term the terms of office shall be staggered so that one 1 councilmember from each ward is elected every two 2 years in the event that a vacancy in office occurs which requires the election of two 2 councilmembers from a ward in the same election the candidate receiving the highest number of votes shall be elected to serve a four 4 year term and the candidate receiving the next highest number of votes shall be elected to serve a two 2 year term at the next regular municipal election and at each subsequent election thereafter the councilmembers to be elected shall serve four 4 year terms  1997   vacancy filling a mayorvacancy in case of the mayors death disability resignation or other vacation of the office the city council shall declare a vacancy in the office of mayor and upon such declaration the city council may order a special election as soon as practicable to fill the vacancy until the term of office of a successor elected at the next regular municipal election has commenced as provided in crs 314105 and the city council may appoint a registered elector in the city of florence to act as mayor until such special election if the city council does not call a special election it shall within sixty 60 days of the declaration of the vacancy fill the vacancy by appointment until the term of the successor elected at the next regular municipal election has commenced crs 314103 b councilmembervacancy if any vacancy occurs in the office of a councilmember because of death resignation removal or for any other reason the city council shall declare a vacancy in the office and shall fill the vacancy by a majority vote of the city council within sixty 60 days from the declaration of the vacancy or by special election as provided in crs 314108b a successor so appointed or elected shall serve until the term of a successor elected at the next regular municipal election has commenced crs 314106  1997   commencement of term following the regular municipal election the term of all newly elected members of the city council including the mayor shall commence at the first meeting of the governing body immediately following the survey of election returns crs 314105  1997  242013   332014 city attorney footnotes  3  for statutory provisions on city attorneys see crs 1973  314208 1975 supp   office created there is created the office of city attorney in the city of florence whose term of office shall be as by law prescribed  1979   powers and duties generally the city attorney shall prosecute all actions upon any ordinance of the city for the recovery of fines and penalties  and as the case may be shall prosecute or defend every action originating or pending before a justice of the peace or in any court to which action the city shall be a party or in which action the official acts of any of its officers or agents shall be involved  provided that without the order of the city council said attorney shall commence no action in the interest of the city except for the violation of a city ordinance  1979   drafting of documents the city attorney shall when required by order of the city council or any committee thereof or any city officer or officers proper in any particular case draft any ordinance contract conveyance or other instrument in writing in relation to the execution of corporate powers or corporate business  1979   legal advisory powers the city attorney shall act as the legal advisor of the city council of the committees of said council and of other city officers in all matters relating to the official powers or duties of such officer or officers or to the corporate business of the city and shall upon request of the mayor furnish an opinion in writing upon any such matter it shall be the duty of said attorney to attend the meetings of the council of which he shall be entitled to notice in like manner as members of the council  1979   executions the city attorney shall cause executions to be issued on judgments recovered in favor of the city and attend to their prompt collection  1979   performance of other duties the city attorney shall perform all such other services in the line of his profession connected with the business of the corporation as shall be required of him by resolution order or ordinance of said council  1979   salary the city attorney shall be paid a salary to be determined from time to time by the city council such payments shall be made on a monthly basis  1979 municipal courts footnotes  4  for statutory provisions on municipal courts see crs 1973  13101011310125  for provisions on trial by jury for petty offenses see crs 1973  1610109   establishment and jurisdiction there shall be a qualified municipal court of record which shall keep a verbatim record of its proceedings and a municipal judge who as a condition of holding this office shall have been admitted to and at all times during his term shall be licensed in the practice of law in colorado preference may be given to a qualified resident of florence for the position of municipal judge the municipal court shall have exclusive original jurisdiction to hear try and determine all cases arising under the ordinances of the city of florence for the violation and enforcement thereof and there shall be no change of venue therefrom  1992 part 1987   municipal judgeappointmentterm of office the municipal judge shall be appointed by the city council after the general election in oddnumbered years the term of office shall be for two 2 years from the date of appointment unless sooner terminated for cause as provided in the colorado revised statutes in effect at said time in the event of a vacancy in the office of municipal judge prior to the expiration of a term of office as set forth herein any appointment shall be for the remainder of the unexpired term city council may also appoint such additional assistant municipal judges as may be necessary to act in case of temporary absence sickness disqualification or other inability of the presiding municipal judge to act the term of such appointment of an assistant judge shall be for the term reasonably deemed necessary as based on the reason for the inability of the presiding municipal judge  1992 part 1987   municipal judgecompensation the salary of the municipal judge shall be established by ordinance upon the appointment of said judge the salary shall be a fixed annual compensation which shall be payable on a monthly or other periodic basis any assistant municipal judges shall receive such compensation as shall be determined at the time of their appointment  1992 part 1987   clerk of the municipal court the municipal judge shall serve as exofficio clerk of the municipal court who shall receive no further or additional compensation for the performance of said duties the municipal judge acting as municipal court clerk shall execute a performance bond as required by colorado revised statutes the cost of which shall be paid by the city part 1987   court facilities and supplies space for court proceedings shall be provided as deemed appropriate by the city council and may include limitations upon court times due to sharing of facilities with other city entities the city council shall provide necessary moneys for supplies necessary to conduct the business of the court at the time of the annual budget preparation part 1987   fines and penalties the municipal judge shall be authorized to impose fines and penalties as provided by ordinances of the city limited by provisions of the colorado revised statutes  part 1987   costs the municipal judge shall be authorized to impose costs of zero to three hundred dollars $000 to $30000 after conviction of an ordinance violation at a trial to the court or to a jury plea of guilty or plea of no contest  1992   surcharge for purchase of police equipment a surcharge in the amount of twenty dollars $2000 shall be imposed against a defendant in addition to all other costs and fines imposed after the defendant is convicted of a municipal ordinance violation at a trial to the court or to a jury plea of guilty or plea of no contests said surcharge is dedicated to the purchase of equipment to be used by the police department and shall be set aside in a separate category within the general fund for this particular purpose k  1 362017   1232012   payment of finestraffic violations the fine schedule set forth in violation of the provisions of the model traffic colorado municipalities may be payable as penalty assessments or the defendant may appear before the judge to enter a plea or have a trial part 1987   fines and costs all fines and costs collected or received by the municipal court shall be reflected in a written receipt a copy of said receipt shall be given to the person delivering the money to the municipal court a copy shall be given to the city clerk and a copy shall be retained in the records of the municipal court each such receipt shall be identified by the name of the defendant and by the citation number all moneys received by the municipal court within one 1 calendar week shall be delivered on or before the close of the first business day of the next calendar week to the city clerk or his authorized agent together with the city clerks copy of all written receipts in the absence of the municipal judge the city clerk or his agent shall be authorized to accept any and all moneys otherwise directed to the municipal court in such case the city clerk or his agent shall prepare a receipt for said moneys with one 1 copy to the municipal judge one 1 copy to the person delivering the money and one 1 copy for the records of the city clerk all moneys received by the city clerk shall be deposited in the general fund of the city of florence part 1987   payment of moneys in the event that moneys must be paid the municipal judge shall request from the city clerk a check drawn on the account of the city of florence to a specific payee and designate the name of the defendant and case number this check shall be ready to be delivered to the designated payee or the municipal judge no later than two 2 business days from the date of the request  part 1987   procedure the municipal court rules of procedure promulgated by the supreme court of the state of colorado from time to time shall govern the procedures in municipal court  part 1987   jury trial fee a defendant waives his right to a jury trial unless within ten 10 days of his arraignment or entry of plea he files a written demand for a jury trial and at the same time tenders to the court a jury fee of twentyfive $2500 dollars unless the fee is waived by the judge because of the indigence of the defendant if the action is dismissed or the defendant is acquitted of the charge or if the defendant having paid a jury fee files with the court at least ten 10 days before the scheduled trial date a written waiver of jury trial the jury fee shall be refunded  part 1987   jury trials for statutory provisions detailing initiative and referendum procedures see crs 1973  140115 et seq  for provisions on the recall of city officers see crs 1973  314501 et seq 1975 supp   powers of the people the legislative power of the city of florence shall be vested as heretofore in the city council subject to the general laws of the state but hereafter the people of said city shall have the power to propose ordinances and to adopt or reject the same at the polls independent of the city council and also shall have the power independent of the city council at their own option to adopt or reject at the polls any ordinance or part of any ordinance adopted by the city council  1913   initiative procedure the initiative power referred to in be exercised by the legal voters of said city whenever fifteen percent 15% of the legal voters desire to propose any ordinance by petition and every such petition shall include the full text of the ordinance proposed such initiative petitions shall be addressed to and filed with the city clerk at least sixty 60 days before the election at which they are to be voted upon  1913   referendum procedure the referendum power referred to in be ordered against any ordinance section or part of any ordinance of the city council by a petition signed by at least ten percent 10% of the legal voters of said city referendum petitions shall likewise be addressed to and filed with the city clerk of the city not more than ninety 90 days after the adoption of the ordinance on which the referendum is demanded the filing of a referendum petition against any section or part of any ordinance shall not delay the remainder of the ordinance from becoming operative  1913   elections to be held at general election all elections on matters of ordinances initiated or referred to the people of the city shall be held at the general election for city officers and all such ordinances shall become a law of the city when approved by a majority of the vote cast thereon and not otherwise and shall take effect from and after the date of the public announcement of the vote thereon by the mayor of said city but not later than thirty 30 days after the vote thereon has been canvassed nothing herein contained shall be construed to deprive the city council of the right to adopt any ordinance subject to the right of referendum herein reserved the whole number of votes cast for mayor of said city at the regular general election last preceding the filing of any petition for the initiative or referendum shall be the basis on which the number of legal votes necessary to sign such petition shall be counted  1913   petitions the city clerk shall submit all ordinances initiated or referred to the people of said city for adoption or rejection at the polls in compliance therewith such petitions for initiating or referring ordinances shall be signed by qualified electors in their own persons only to which shall be attached the residence address of such person and the date of signing the same to each of such petitions there shall be attached an affidavit of some qualified elector of said city that each signature thereon is the signature of the person whose name it purports to be and that to the best of the knowledge and belief of the affiant each of the persons signing said petition was at the time of signing a qualified elector of said city such petition so verified shall be prima facie evidence that the signatures thereon are genuine and true and that the persons signing the same are qualified electors  1913   the style of all ordinances adopted by the people initiative shall be be it ordained by the people of the city of florence  1913   recallestablished every elective officer of the city of florence may be recalled from office at any time by the electors entitled to vote for his successor and such procedure shall be known as the recall and it shall be an additional method for the removal of officers in addition to other methods provided by law s7 1913   recallprocedure a the procedure to effect the recall of any elective officer shall be as follows a petition signed by electors qualified to vote for a successor of the incumbent equal in number to twentyfive percent 25% of the total vote cast at the last preceding election for all candidates to the office which the incumbent sought to be recalled occupies demanding the removal of said officer and the election of his successor as provided by law shall be filed with the city clerk  and such petition shall contain a general statement in not more than two hundred 200 words of the ground or grounds on which such recall is sought which statement shall be made for the information of the electors and the electors shall be the sole judges of the legality reasonableness and sufficiency of the ground or grounds assigned for such recall and said ground or grounds shall not be open to review signatures need not be all on the same page of paper but if more than one page is necessary they must be securely fastened and the ground or grounds must be read by the signers each separately and the signer must subscribe after his name the date of his signing and the number or place of his residence and he must sign the same of his own free and voluntary act and without intimidation payment or promise of reward and the person circulating such petition must make and subscribe an oath on each sheet of signatures thereof that the signatures thereon are genuine and a false oath wilfully so made and subscribed by such person shall be perjury and be punished as such all petitions shall be deemed and held to be sufficient as they appear to be signed by the persons whose names are subscribed and a sufficient number of signers appear thereon giving the dates of their signature and their street number providing the same shall be within the territory required as above provided and all signers shall be deemed to be qualified electors unless a protest in writing under oath shall be filed in the office of the city clerk within fifteen l5 days after the petition is filed after such protest is filed setting forth the grounds thereof the city clerk shall forthwith mail a copy of such protest to the person or persons named and against whose signatures protest is made with a notice of the time for hearing such protest which shall not be less than five 5 nor more than ten 10 days after the mailing of such notice such hearings shall be before the mayor of the city unless he should be a party affected by said recall in which event it shall be before the police magistrate of the city all testimony offered on hearing of protests shall be under oath the proceedings shall be prompt and without delay and be determined within not more than three 3 days from the date set for hearing the sufficiency of the grounds of the petition for recall shall in no manner be considered by the mayor or police magistrate and their finding as to the qualifications or sufficiency in number of signers shall be final if the number of qualified signers is found to be insufficient the petition may be recalled and again filed with sufficient additional names if the same be done within fifteen 15 days and it shall then be considered as a new petition filed b the above petition for recall having been filed and there being no protests to the sufficiency of the signers thereon or the same having been disposed of as herein provided so leaving the petition unchallenged the said petition shall at the first meeting of the city council occurring not less than fifteen 15 days after the filing of said petition be referred to the city council and a record thereof shall be spread upon the minutes of their proceedings c if the person or persons against whom recall petition has been filed shall tender their resignation the same shall be accepted and the vacancy filled as provided by statute for the filling of such vacancies but if such officer sought to be recalled shall not resign within five 5 days after said petition of recall is submitted to the city council the city council shall by resolution call a special election to be conducted in accordance with the laws governing elections in municipalities to vote upon the question of the recall of such officer or officers against whom petitions of recall are on file and for the election of their successors  1913   statutes adopted except as otherwise provided in this chapter the laws rules and regulations provided by the statutes of the state of colorado for the initiative and referendum and the recall of officers and the election of their successors are adoptedso far as the same may be applicable and are made the law rules and regulations governing the initiative and referendum and the second reading to avoid a lapse in the propertycasualty insurance coverage for the city of florence part 1996 employee legal defense policy   purpose the purpose of this chapter is to create a local policy for the legal defense of employees of the city of florence named as defendants in civil suits to the extent such a policy is consistent with colorado revised statutes as amended and the colorado constitution part 1995   scope and definitions a the colorado governmental immunity act the act provides that the city under certain circumstances must assume the cost of defending its employees and paying judgments and settlements against its employees this policy implements the provisions of the act and applies to the same extent as the act this policy also applies to claims brought under federal law as provided by the act b as used in this policy claim means a civil action brought in state or federal court which is subject to the act or which is based on a federal law and lies in tort as defined in the act c as used in this policy employee shall have the same meaning as provided in 4 crs as amended and shall include a former employee of the city d by adopting this policy the city is expressly not waiving any immunities or monetary limits under crs et seq as amended colorado governmental immunity act or any other immunities as are established by law e this policy is to be construed consistent with of the colorado constitution tabor  and is not to be construed as a multiyear obligation but rather as a policy to be reviewed on an annual basis part 1995   policy cost of defense the city shall be liable for the reasonable costs including reasonable attorneys fees of the defense of an employee against a claim if a the city attorney determines that the claim arose out of injuries sustained from an act or omission of the employee occurring or alleged in the complaint to have occurred during the performance of the employees duties and within the scope of the employees employment with the city  and b the city attorney determines that the employees act or omission was not willful or wanton  and c the employee does not compromise or settle the claim without the written consent of this city council  and d the employee provided written notice to the city council city attorney of the incident or occurrence which led to the claim within a reasonable time after the incident or occurrence if the incident or occurrence could reasonably have been expected to lead to a claim  and e in the case of an action to which the city is not a party defendant the employee provided written notice to the city council city attorney of existence of the action against the employee within fifteen 15 days after the commencement of the action part 1995   legal representation for employee the city shall have met any responsibility it may have under the services of the attorney assigned by the insurance entity which provides a defense for the claim or services of the city attorney or a different attorney selected by the city nothing herein shall prohibit an employee from retaining the services of his or her own attorney but except as otherwise provided in the fees and costs of those services shall be borne solely by the employee part 1995   payment of judgments and settlements of claims against city employees the city shall be liable for the payment of all judgments and settlements of claims against a city employee under the circumstances specified in a e but only if sovereign immunity would not bar the action against the city however if such immunity would otherwise bar the action against the city the city shall still remain responsible pursuant to this section to pay any judgment or settlement of a claim against an employee where the action arose out of the employees operation of an emergency vehicle and the employee was operating the vehicle within the provisions of 2 and 3 crs part 1995   employee responsibility a any employee involved in an incident or occurrence in which any person may have been injured or any physical damage to property may have occurred as a result of an act or omission of the employee occurring during the performance of the employees duties shall as soon as practicable but in any event within seventytwo 72 hours following the incident or occurrence notify or have a supervisor notify the city council city attorney of the incident or occurrence b if a civil action is filed against a city employee and the action contains any claim of injury to a person or to property from an act or omission of the employee occurring during the performance of the employees duties or within the scope of the employees employment with the city the employee or the employees supervisor shall provide written notice to the city council city attorney of the existence of the civil action within fifteen 15 days after the commencement of the action the employee or the employees supervisor shall promptly transmit to the city council city attorney a copy of the complaint served on the employee c the employee shall not compromise or settle any claim unless the city council has notified the employee in writing that the city will not bear the cost of the legal defense of a civil action against the employee if an employee violates this provision the city will not be responsible for payment of the employees costs attorney fees judgments or settled claims part 1995   notification to employee a within a reasonable time after receipt by the city council of any written notice provided pursuant to the city attorney shall notify the employee in writing whether the city will assume the defense of the employee b if the city is made codefendant with an employee in a civil action the city attorney shall notify the employee in writing within a reasonable time after the commencement of the action whether the city will assume the defense of the employee part 1995   reimbursement of expenses if a defense is provided pursuant to this policy in an action filed against an employee and the trial court determines that the injuries did not arise out of an act or omission of the employee occurring during the performance of the employees duties and within the scope of the employees employment or that the act or omission of the employee was willful and wanton the employee shall reimburse the city for reasonable costs and reasonable attorneys fees incurred in the defense of the employee part 1995   conflicts of interest in the event that an attorney who represents both the city and the employee pursuant to that representation of both would create a conflict of interest separate counsel shall be appointed pursuant to each party part 1995   reimbursement of punitive damages the city is not liable for punitive damages which are awarded against an employee nor is the city required to defend an employee against a claim for punitive damages unless the city council in its sole discretion determines otherwise pursuant to the procedure set forth in 5 crs as amended part 1995   severability clause if any section or sections of this chapter or the application thereof to any person or circumstances is declared unconstitutional or otherwise invalid by any court of competent jurisdiction such invalidity shall not affect other sections of this chapter or their application if they can be given effect without the invalid section or sections and to such extent the sections of this chapter are declared severable part 1995 title 3  revenue and finance chapters fiscal year fiscal year designated the fiscal year for the city of florence shall correspond with the calendar year each beginning with the first day of january of each year  1932 sales tax purpose and statutory authority the purpose of this chapter is to impose a sales tax on the sale of the tangible personal property at retail or the furnishing of services as provided in title 29 and title 39 colorado revised statutes 197 as amended upon every retailer in the city of florence  1978   definitions for the purpose of this chapter words contained in this chapter shall be defined in title 39 colorado revised statutes 197 as amended and such definitions are incorporated herein by this reference  1978   license required it is unlawful for any person or legal entity to engage in the business of selling tangible personal property at retail within the incorporated city without first having obtained a license therefor such license shall be granted and issued by the city clerk and shall be in force and effect until the thirtyfirst 31st day of december of the year in which it is issued unless sooner revoked the initial license for persons engaged in business as defined in  on  shall be obtained prior to   1978   application for license such license shall be granted and renewed only upon application stating the name and address of the person desiring such a license the name of such business and the location and such other facts as the city clerk may require  1978   renewal of license it shall be the duty of each licensee on or before january first 1st of each year during which this chapter remains in effect to obtain a renewal thereof if the licensee remains in the retail business or liable to account for the tax herein provided  nothing herein contained shall be construed to empower the city clerk to refuse such renewal except revocation for cause of the licensees prior license  1978   separate license required for each place of business in case business is transacted at one or more separate premises by one person a separate license for each place of business shall be required  1978   selling without license deemed violation any person engaged in the business of selling tangible personal property at retail in the city of florence without having secured a license therefor except as specifically provided herein shall be guilty of a violation of this chapter  1978   contents of license each license shall be numbered and shall show the name residence place and character of business of the licensee and shall be posted in a conspicuous place in the place of business for which it is issued no license shall be transferable  1978   certain commodities deemed exempt no license shall be required for any person engaged exclusively in the business of selling commodities which are exempt from taxation under this  1978   statutes adopted by reference for the purpose of collection administration and enforcement of this chapter by the director of revenue the provisions of colorado revised statutes 197 as amended exemptions disputes credits or refunds shall be deemed applicable and incorporated into this chapter  1978   amount not to include state sales and use tax the amount subject to tax under this chapter shall not include the state sales and use tax imposed by title 39 colorado revised statutes 197 as amended  1978   consummation of sales for the purpose of this chapter all retail sales shall be considered consummated at the place of business of the retailer unless the tangible personal property sold is delivered by the retailer or his agent to a destination outside the city of florence or to a common carrier for delivery to a destination outside the limits of the city of florence  1978   gross receipts to include delivery charges the gross receipts from sales shall include delivery charges when such charges are subject to the state sales and use tax imposed by title 39 colorado revised statutes 197 as amended regardless of the this chapter extend or apply a to the storage use or consumption of any tangible personal property the sale of which is subject to the retail sales tax imposed by of this code  b to the storage use or business  c to the storage use or consumption of tangible personal property brought into the city by a nonresident thereof for his own storage use or consumption while temporarily within the city of any article of tangible personal property the sale or use of which has already been subjected to a sales or use tax of another county city or town equal to or in excess of that imposed by this the amount of the credit shall be equal to the tax paid by him by reason of the imposition of a sales tax or use tax of another county city or town on his purchase or use of the property the amount of building permit by the city building inspector c should either the building permit applicant or the city feel that the deposit provided for in subsection b of this section does not accurately reflect the actual amount of the use tax owed by the applicant when the calculation of the use tax shall be made based upon an affidavit which shall be submitted to the city clerk sworn to by the building permit applicant and supported by adequate documentation to verify the amount of tax owed the building permit applicant shall be required to maintain and preserve detailed receipts and purchase possession of or under the control of the municipality part 1992   definitions unless otherwise required by context or use words and terms shall be defined as follows municipality means the city of florence colorado owner means a person or entity including a corporation partnership association governmental entity other than this municipality or a duly authorized legal representative or successor in interest of same which owns unclaimed property held by the municipality unclaimed property means any tangible or intangible property including any income or increment derived therefrom less any lawful charges that is held by or under the control of the municipality and which has not been claimed by its owner for a period of more than five years after it became payable or distributable part 1992   procedure for notification of owner a prior to disposition of any unclaimed property having an estimated value of fifty dollars $5000 or more the city manager shall send a written notice by certified mail return receipt requested to the last known address if any of any owner of unclaimed property the last known address of the owner shall be the last address of the owner as shown by the records of the municipal department or agency holding the property the notice shall include a description of the property the amount or estimated value of the property and when available the purpose for which the property was deposited or otherwise held and designating a place and time for the public sale of said property if a sale is necessary the notice shall state where the owner may make inquiry of or claim the property the notice shall also state that if the owner fails to provide the city manager with a written claim for the return of the property prior to the time fixed in said notice for the public sale of said property or within sixty 60 days of the date of the notice if a sale is not necessary the property shall become the sole property of the municipality and any claim of the owner to such property shall be deemed forfeited b prior to disposition of any unclaimed property having an estimated value of less than fifty dollars $5000 or having no last known address of the owner the city manager shall cause a notice to be published one time in the municipalitys official newspaper the notice shall include a description of the property the presumed owner of the property if known the amount or estimated value of the property and when available the purpose for which the property was deposited or otherwise held and designating a place and time for the public sale of said property if a sale is necessary the notice shall state where the owner may make inquiry of or claim the property the notice shall also state that if the owner fails to provide the city manager with a written claim for the return of the property prior to the time fixed in said notice for the public sale of said property or within sixty 60 days of the date of the publication of the notice if a sale is not necessary the property shall become the sole property of the municipality and any claim of the owner to such property shall be deemed forfeited part 1992   delivery to owner a in case any property shall come into the custody of the city and be claimed by any person as provided in it shall be the duty of the city manager to make such inquiry and examination as to the ownership of the property as he or she may deem necessary and if he or she is satisfied that the property belongs to the person claiming the same he or she is authorized to release the property to such owner upon the owner giving a proper receipt therefor b in the event that there is more than one claimant for the same property the city manager may in the city managers sole discretion resolve said claims or may resolve such claims by depositing the disputed property with the registry of the district court in an interpleader action c any legal action filed challenging a decision of the city manager shall be filed pursuant to rule 106 of the colorado rules of civil procedure within thirty 30 days of such decision or shall be forever barred if any legal action is timely filed the property shall be disbursed by the city manager pursuant to the order of the court having jurisdiction over such claim d no property subject to return shall be released to any owner until the municipality has been reimbursed for all reasonable expenses of custody and handling thereof including costs of mailing and publication part 1992   sale of property in general if property in the possession of the municipality is not claimed by the rightful owner as provided in the property shall be sold at public sale at the time and place mentioned in the notice it shall be the duty of the city manager to sell all such unclaimed property for the highest and best price the same will bring in cash to receive from the purchaser of each and every article the amount paid by such purchaser for the same and to deliver the article together with a bill of sale for the same to the purchaser part 1992   report of sale and disposition of proceeds the city manager shall from time to time make reports to the city council as he or she deems necessary of sales provided for in this chapter such reports shall give a description of articles sold and the amount of money received for the articles which money shall be placed in the general fund of the municipality part 1992   disposition of unsold property the city manager is authorized to dispose of any and all property not sold at a public sale conducted as provided in this chapter at any time thereafter at his or her discretion any proceeds derived therefrom to be placed in the general fund of the city part 1992   disposition of property with minimal value notwithstanding any other provision of this chapter to the contrary certain items of property having a minimal value which are not suitable for sale in the discretion of the city manager and which can be used for the publics benefit may be donated to a recognized charitable institution if directed by the city manager without having to comply with the provisions of this chapter such items may include but are not necessarily limited to toys clothing bedding and personal care items part 1992   disposition of unclaimed intangible property all intangible property subject to disposition under this chapter which is held in any fund of the municipality at the time such property becomes the property of the municipality under shall be distributed to such fund all other intangible property held by the municipality which is subject to disposition under this chapter shall be distributed to the general fund part 1992   exceptions the provisions of this chapter shall not apply to the sale of abandoned automobile as governed by title 42 crs 1973 as amended  the disposition of lost or stray animals as governed by title 35 crs 1973 as amended  the disposition of property seized confiscated or forfeited by a municipal seizing agency governed by title 16 and title 18 crs 1973 as amended part 1992   failure to claim property failure to timely make claim of ownership within the time prescribed in shall forever bar the owner or any person claiming ownership by or under the owner from any property rights in the property in issue part 1992   escheat if no person establishes a right to any property as required under the property shall escheat to the municipality and the owner or any person who alleges that he or she is entitled to the property shall be forever barred from any and all claim or right to such property or the proceeds of sale therefrom part 1992   severability if any part section subsection sentence clause or phrase of the ordinance codified in this chapter is for any reason held to be invalid such invalidity shall not affect the validity of the remaining sections of this ordinance the city council declares that it would have passed the ordinance 1982 seizureforfeiture fund establishment there is established for the convenience and proper administration of the affairs of the city a fund of the city which shall be known as the seizureforfeiture fund part 1997   composition the seizureforfeiture fund shall consist of such sums of money that are delivered to and received by or on behalf of the florence police department with respect to law enforcement activities that resulted in the seizure or forfeiture of real or personal property pursuant to applicable federal or state laws the moneys to be deposited in this fund may include without limitation any sums payable to and received by or on behalf of the florence police department as a seizing agency from state of colorado sources identified at parts 3 and 5 of title 16 crs  or from federal sources pursuant to federal laws rules and regulations the receipt use and disposition of which are authorized by crs part 1997   special provisions a the seizureforfeiture fund is designated as the lawfully created fund to receive proceeds from property seized by andor forfeited to the federal or state government and allocated to the florence police department pursuant to federal or state laws and regulations b for accounting purposes the seizureforfeiture fund shall be treated as a special reserve account which will have two 2 divisions one 1 such division shall receive proceeds from property seized by andor forfeited to the federal government and allocated by an agency or officer of the unites states government  and the other division shall receive proceeds from property seized by andor forfeited to the state of colorado pursuant to state law the assets of each division shall not be commingled c all seized andor forfeited property and all proceeds from seized andor forfeited property received by or on behalf of the florence police department shall be subject to the reporting and audit requirements set forth at crs d all such seized andor forfeited property and all proceeds from seized andor forfeited property received by or on behalf of the florence police department shall be used and expended only as approved and authorized by the committee on disposition required under crs and established by the further provisions of this chapter no expenditure shall be authorized except by a majority vote of all of the members of the committee a written memorandum regarding each expenditure authorized by the committee shall be made and shall reflect the vote of each committee member e pursuant to 3 crs the committee on disposition for the florence police department shall at a minimum be required to be comprised of the district attorney of the eleventh judicial district or his designee the chief of police of the city of florence or his designee and the mayor of the city of florence additional members may be selected to serve on the committee by the unanimous agreement of the required members pursuant to 3 crs the committee is specifically authorized to establish and maintain one 1 or more bank accounts to be used for law enforcement purposes designated by the committee and to deposit into such account or accounts assets of the seizureforfeiture fund f in accordance with applicable federal and state laws moneys in the seizureforfeiture fund shall not be subject to appropriation by the city council of the city of florence nor shall such moneys be used or expended for any purpose that is prohibited by applicable federal or state laws or for any permitted purpose that is not specifically authorized by the committee g any interest or other revenue generated on account of investment of moneys in the seizureforfeiture fund shall remain in the fund part 1997 capital acquisition and improvement fund capital acquisition and improvement fund of building permit fees as assessed under the florence municipal part 2005   definitions for purposes of this chapter the following words shall have the meanings ascribed to them as follows business owner means a natural person firm association partnership trust corporation limited liability company or other legal entity that carries on a commercial enterprise for profit or a particular forprofit occupation or employment habitually engaged in for livelihood or gain business owner hereunder shall not include the owner of a homebased business capital investment costs mean land acquisition costs as well as the gross cost of all structures buildings fixtures fences parking lots and the like erected upon or affixed to the land as determined by the city manager capital investment costs by a business owner shall not include land acquisition and other development costs of a project that is primarily for residential purposes as determined by the city manager part 2005   rebate a a business owner shall be entitled to a rebate of fortyfive 45 percent of the building permit fee actually paid pursuant to this code so long as the capital investment costs of the project as defined at this chapter exceed one hundred fifty thousand dollars $15000000 as determined by the city manager b such rebate shall be paid to the business owner coincident with the issuance of a final certificate of occupancy as authorized by the city manager c the effective date of the ordinance codified in this chapter shall be  part 2005 title 5  business licenses and regulations chapters footnotes  1  for statutory provisions authorizing cities to tax license and regulate businesses see crs  3115501  for provisions regarding licenses for tree trimmers see ch 1228 of this code  for provisions on trailer park licenses see ch 1536 of this code licensing of businesses   definitions a business means and includes each kind of vocation occupation profession enterprise and establishment or any and all other kind of activity and matter any of which are conducted for private profit or benefit either directly or indirectly on any premises within the city or anywhere else within its jurisdiction and shall also mean and include all devices machines vehicles and appurtenances used therein a business which does not make any sales transactions exchanges trades deliveries or shipments of goods or services within the city is not subject to this definition and does not need a business license b casual transaction is an isolated single or incidental transaction which in itself does not constitute the carrying on of business examples include but are not limited to fund raisers  garage sales  bake sales  or private sale of a vehicle c city means the city of florence colorado d fixed business is any business operating from a set operating location fixed business does not include a home occupation e license means a business license f licensee is any person required to obtain a license g home occupation is any business operated from a residence no home occupation shall be allowed on property zoned as commercial as the same is defined in the city zoning of home occupations include but are not limited to licensed day care facilities  accountants  hairdressers  attorneys  and seamstresses h nonfixed business is any established business not having a set operating location within the city statutes lpart 1988   suspension or revocationfine a whenever a decision of the city council acting as the local licensing authority suspending a retail license for fourteen 14 days or less becomes final whether by failure of the retail licensee to appeal the decision or by exhaustion of all appeals and judicial review the retail licensee may before the operative date of the suspension petition the city council acting as the local licensing authority for permission to pay a fine in lieu of having his retail license suspended for all or part of the suspension period upon the receipt of the petition the city council acting as the local licensing authority may at its sole discretion stay the proposed suspension and cause any investigation to be made which it deems desirable and may in its sole discretion grant the petition if it is satisfied 1 that the public welfare and morals would not be impaired by permitting the retail licensee to operate during the period set for suspension and that the payment of the fine will achieve the desired disciplinary purposes  2 that the books and records of the retail licensee are kept in such a manner that the loss of sales of alcoholic beverages which the retail licensee would have suffered had the suspension gone into effect can be determined with reasonable accuracy therefrom  and 3 that the retail licensee has not had his license suspended or revoked nor had any suspension stayed by payment of a fine during the two 2 years immediately preceding the date of the motion or complaint which has resulted in a final decision to suspend the retail license b the fine accepted shall be equivalent to twenty percent 20% of the retail licensees estimated gross revenues from sales of alcoholic beverages during the period of the proposed suspension  except that the fine shall be not less than two hundred dollars $20000 nor more than five thousand dollars $500000 c payment of any fine pursuant to the provisions of this section shall be in the form of cash certified check or cashiers check made payable to the city of florence and shall be deposited in the general fund of the city of florence d upon payment of the fine pursuant to this section the city council acting as the local licensing authority shall enter its further order permanently staying the imposition of the suspension e in connection with any petition pursuant to this section the authority of the city council acting as the local licensing authority is limited to the granting of such stays as are necessary for it to complete its investigation and make its findings and if it makes such findings to the granting of an order permanently staying the imposition of the entire suspension or that portion of the suspension not otherwise conditionally stayed f if the city council acting as the local licensing authority does not make the findings required in subsection a of this section and does not order the suspension permanently stayed the suspension shall
